<li>But the nous, once it is  joined with the human soul, becomes a single substance with her through an  intimate fusion, so that such souls are nevermore obscured by the delusions of  darkness.51 Clearly this means that nous cannot be identical to the common capacity  of “mind,” “intellect,” or “consciousness” that all human beings have  in common: for the latter, our passage uses a different word, mens.52 By    50   Banner, Philosophic Silence, 187 (here more specifically about noēsis, the activity of  nous). <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_84">[eref]</span></li>
<li>Banner’s subtle analysis of nous and noēsis in Plotinus (ibid., Chapter 6) is  of the greatest relevance here. <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_84">[eref]</span></li>
<li>The Hermetic references to nous read very much like simplified popular  echoes of Plotinus’ technical discussions. <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_84">[eref]</span></li>
<li>It is crucial to distinguish between two ways  in which nous is understood: ontologically as primary being (ousia, as distinct from  the One above being: Banner, Philosophic Science, 183), and epistemologically as the  capacity to access or comprehend that being though noēsis. <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_84">[eref]</span></li>
<li>… Nous is an intelligible world, and also acts as a fac- ulty of noēsis; but there is only one nous, which is both of these things” (ibid., 196;  same point in Van den Kerchove, La voie, 29; I find Banner’s remarks apply equally  to the Hermetica). <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_84">[eref]</span></li>
<li>52     Note that the standard Latin translation of nous in the Ascl <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_84">[eref]</span></li>
<li>The Presence of Gods 61 contrast, nous must refer to a higher capacity for noēsis that is active  or awake in only a small minority of spiritually “enlightened” human  beings.53 For them, it becomes like an interior sun that illuminates their  soul so permanently and completely (through an “intimate fusion” that  is never interrupted once it is there) that no room is left in it for delusion- ary shadows.54 We are not dealing here with a spiritual elitism according  to which only a few human beings are privileged to have nous and are  capable of finding salvation. <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_85">[eref]</span></li>
<li>Rather, the universal divine Source has gen- erously made the gift of nous available to all human beings,55 but the sad  reality is that only few of them show any interest. <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_85">[eref]</span></li>
<li>Most people are living  lives that make them simply incapable of receiving it: they allow them- selves to be “deceived by delusionary images”56 rather than cultivating  their potential for receiving nous. <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_85">[eref]</span></li>
<li>It should be noted that even if nous illu- minates the inner universe of the human soul with divine light, still this  does not necessarily imply perfect or absolute knowledge of transcendent  reality in its true essence; rather, “human beings can perceive the things  that are in heaven as if through a mist, in so far as the condition of the  human nous permits it.”57 Direct and wholly unobscured knowledge of  the absolute requires an extra step towards a unitive experience beyond  logos and the internal senses, as will be seen.58 Terrestrial Gods By no means should the Asclepius be understood as a mere theoretical  exposition of how everything in the world is hanging together. <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_85">[eref]</span></li>
<li>Look at your incredulity… You are talk- ing about beings endowed with nous and spirit [pneuma] and call them  ‘statues’…”62 What is going on here? <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_86">[eref]</span></li>
<li>3 and 19 (translation Kingsley, “An Introduction,” 38–39; because sensus in the  Asclepius means nous, I prefer “divine noetic concentration” over “divine concentration  of consciousness”). <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_86">[eref]</span></li>
<li>That Asclepius does not understand the true nature of the gods is con- firmed later on, when he refers to them as mere “statues,” using Latin  and Coptic words that suggest they are really just matter.69 On the con- trary, Hermes exclaims, they are living beings endowed with nous and  spirit! <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_88">[eref]</span></li>
<li>Those gods are really  and quite literally “living beings endowed with nous and spirit” just  like themselves. <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_89">[eref]</span></li>
<li>Believe me: to be devoted to the religion of nous will even  constitute a capital crime. <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_-_hermetic_spirituality_and_the_historical_imagination_altered_states_of_knowledge_in_late_antiqui:page_98">[eref]</span></li>
<li><span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: Cam- bridge, MA: Harvard University Press, 1972">[eref]</span>, 2: 642-52, here 645) evades che problem by cranslacing &quot;wich Nous.&quot; @ 49 Cí CH: IV. <span class="entity-pill" title="Source fragment: wouter_j_hanegraaff_ruud_m_bouthoorn_lodovico_lazzarelli_the_hermetic_writings_and_related_documen:page_205">[eref]</span></li>
</ul>
